Nick and Nate MADE a family, a community,  out of their friends and students. What he says in this interview about wanting to take 10 of his people with him into the UFC shows how much the "Nick Diaz Army" means to him.   The Diaz brothers are a rarity. They are exceptionally skilled and tough fighters that refuse to use steroids even when most fighters are. In their view, becoming a champion via PED's is illegitimate. What Nate says in this interview is very true, he gets injured but has never lost a fight and simply runs out of rounds. Nick very similarly also, never KO'd or submitted. That makes them GOAT's.  The mindset is that they are both already champions minus the title. Nate also makes some great points here about his legacy and neither he or his brother were ever given many opportunities to fight for a title despite fighting top 5 ranked guys for years and despite their longevity in the sport (not to mention their popularity with fans.) The UFC may have thrown him to the wolves with this Khamzat fight, but in Nate's mind he is frustrated that the fights he tried to make that he knew the fans would want, never got made for his last fight. He is clear: He didn't want Khamzat but accepted because he will fight anyone and wants to be a free agent.  I wish him the best for his family, his little girl and his wife. I hope he beats Khamzat and walks away from the sport and focuses on his ventures; Real Fight INC, his weed business and the Academy and his coaching. Equally, I hope Nick (if he does decide to return to the UFC) comes back strong for one of two big payday fights: McGregor would be a good one tbh, although I know people are saying that's not the fight to make. It would be nice to see Nick make some $ after such a huge layoff and retire after showing the world again just how good a fighter he is. Although equally, be happy to see him focus on his Academy and start a family. I think married life and children would fill a void in him, personally. He'd make a good father I believe.
